  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_25958fc8-43dd-4612-bfdf-7056461b14e9'
      });
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer3057238453048227812"><b>A New York Times Bestseller</b><br/><br/>Kyle Keeley is the class clown, popular with most kids, (if not the teachers), and an ardent fan of all games: board games, word games, and particularly video games.   <span id="freeText3057238453048227812" style="display:none"><b>A New York Times Bestseller</b><br /><br />Kyle Keeley is the class clown, popular with most kids, (if not the teachers), and an ardent fan of all games: board games, word games, and particularly video games. His hero, Luigi Lemoncello, the most notorious and creative gamemaker in the world, just so happens to be the genius behind the building of the new town library.<br /><br />Lucky Kyle wins a coveted spot to be one of the first 12 kids in the library for an overnight of fun, food, and lots and lots of games. But when morning comes, the doors remain locked. Kyle and the other winners must solve every clue and every secret puzzle to find the hidden escape route. And the stakes are very high.<br /><br />In this cross between <i>Charlie and the Chocolate Factory</i> and <i>A Night in the Museum,</i> Agatha Award winner Chris Grabenstein uses rib-tickling humor to create the perfect tale for his quirky characters. Old fans and new readers will become enthralled with the crafty twists and turns of this ultimate library experience.</span>

<div id="review_743631934" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/743631934" />
    <a title="karen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45618-karen"><img alt="karen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596291582p2/45618.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/743631934?book_show_action=true">Oct 17, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="karen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="karen" href="/user/show/45618-karen">karen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=mg-booknerds">mg-booknerds</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=books-about-books-about-books">books-about-books-about-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer743631934" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7246035788717368922">this is the <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6310.Charlie_and_the_Chocolate_Factory__Charlie_Bucket___1_' title='Charlie and the Chocolate Factory (Charlie Bucket, #1) by Roald Dahl' rel='nofollow noopener'>Charlie and the Chocolate Factory</a> for book- and puzzle-nerds. or, as one character says, "It'll be like <i>The Hunger Games</i> but with lots of food and no bows or arrows."<br/><br/>it takes place in alexandriaville, ohio (not a real place, but a real cutesy reference, one of many peppering this book), whose town library was demolished 12 years ago. a wealthy eccentric gentleman who made his fortune creating a series of very popular games and puzzles decides to rebuild the library and engineers an e</span>
  <span id="freeText7246035788717368922" style="display:none">this is the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6310.Charlie_and_the_Chocolate_Factory__Charlie_Bucket___1_" title="Charlie and the Chocolate Factory (Charlie Bucket, #1) by Roald Dahl" rel="nofollow noopener">Charlie and the Chocolate Factory</a> for book- and puzzle-nerds. or, as one character says, "It'll be like <i>The Hunger Games</i> but with lots of food and no bows or arrows."<br><br>it takes place in alexandriaville, ohio (not a real place, but a real cutesy reference, one of many peppering this book), whose town library was demolished 12 years ago. a wealthy eccentric gentleman who made his fortune creating a series of very popular games and puzzles decides to rebuild the library and engineers an elaborate publicity stunt where twelve children from the town, all twelve years of age, who have never had the pleasure of browsing through the stacks of a public library, are selected to participate in a lock-in and encouraged to solve a series of puzzles to "escape" the library and win a fabulous prize. these are three of my favorite things: puzzles, books, and lock-ins.<br><br>i can't imagine growing up in a town without a library. i am from the smallest state of them all, from a wee village, but there was a town library reasonably close that i could walk to in the summer when i was a teenager. when i was too young to walk there, i used to be driven - dropped off, actually, while my parents ran errands or tried to obtain the paperwork necessary for trading me in for a horse (an oft-used threat in my house). but i grew up in those stacks, making my way from the picture books to the chapter books to the adult books, there not being much in the way of teen fiction when i was that age. so it was heartwarming indeed for me to follow these characters as they experience the thrills of the library for the first time, even though this library is way cooler than any library that actually exists, with holograms of tigers and all. <br><br>and grabenstein is smart - this is librarian-bait like crazy. librarians love books about librarians, and books that teach kids how cool the library is, and kids love fast-paced books filled with puzzles to solve. it's pretty much win-win.<br><br>is is a perfect book? nah - the characters are pretty stock, the outcome predictable, and the puzzles are not as cool as those in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/52092-liza-bill-jed-mysteries" rel="nofollow noopener">my beloved peggy parish series</a>.<br><br>but it does teach kids how to use the library: how the dewey decimal system works, what the archives are, how to ask a librarian for help, and there is also a lot of trivia about literature and A LOT of book-title name-dropping, which would have thrilled me as a little girl and would have made me take out a little pencil and mini-notebook to write down each and every title so i could read those books as well. nerd alert!<br><br>speaking of nerd alert - in this book, i am totally sierra. more excited to be in a building full of books than playing/winning a contest?? curled up reading while everyone else is running around playing games?? yeah, that sounds familiar. i spent a lot of my summer camp days curled up reading under the piano while everyone else just went nuts making stuff with pipe cleaners and singing along with the radio. <br><br>but while it does have its flaws, it is still super-super fun, and any book that makes the library sound like THE place to be is okay by me. plus there are many examples of how not to be a jerk, which can get a little cloying and unrealistic at times, but are probably useful because the world already has enough jerks. plus: BOOKS!! PUZZLES!! LOCK-INS!!<br><br>fun times one million.<br><br>oh, and this is the author's note:<br><br><i>Is the game really over?<br>Maybe not.<br>There is one more puzzle in the book that wasn't in the story. (Although a clue about how to find it was!)<br>If you figure out the solution, let me know.</i><br><br>and then he gives his email address. <br><br>and so now i have to read it again, because i wanna solve this hidden puzzle!<br><br>very smart, indeed, grabenstein…very. smart. indeed.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1528725630i/25720315.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><a href="http://bloggycomelately.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">come to my blog!</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="7246035788717368922" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_794188047" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/794188047" />
    <a title="Marjorie Ingall" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1249329-marjorie-ingall"><img alt="Marjorie Ingall" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1529365795p2/1249329.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/794188047?book_show_action=true">Dec 19, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marjorie Ingall" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marjorie Ingall" href="/user/show/1249329-marjorie-ingall">Marjorie Ingall</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1249329-marjorie-ingall?shelf=kids-9-12">kids-9-12</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer794188047" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3868832025720749327">WHAT IS WRONG WITH YOU EVERYONE WHO LIKED THIS I FEEL LIKE DONALD SUTHERLAND IN INVASION OF TEH BODY SNATCHERS YOU ARE ALL PODS. <br/><br/>It gets one star because it has the word LIBRARY in the title. I like libraries.<br/><br/>But Chris Grabenstein does not. At least, he doesn't like libraries qua libraries. His version of an ideal library is like being floo-powdered into World of Warcraft then spiked with Disneyland and dosed with Ritalin. The book talks the talk about the awesomeness of libraries but then shows</span>
  <span id="freeText3868832025720749327" style="display:none">WHAT IS WRONG WITH YOU EVERYONE WHO LIKED THIS I FEEL LIKE DONALD SUTHERLAND IN INVASION OF TEH BODY SNATCHERS YOU ARE ALL PODS. <br /><br />It gets one star because it has the word LIBRARY in the title. I like libraries.<br /><br />But Chris Grabenstein does not. At least, he doesn't like libraries qua libraries. His version of an ideal library is like being floo-powdered into World of Warcraft then spiked with Disneyland and dosed with Ritalin. The book talks the talk about the awesomeness of libraries but then shows-don't-tells that libraries need to be TV. <br /><br />The characters are pancake-flat. The dialogue is crawl-under-the-rug lame. I was a mature enough parent that I did not suggest a drinking game involving doing a shot every time Miguel Fernandez said "bro," BUT I THOUGHT IT. The whole enterprise just seemed so CYNICAL, a naked ploy to sell books to librarians by sucking up to them while actually pulling the beeping/flashing/green-screened wool over their eyes. It depressed me. It name-dropped a zillion book titles without ever conveying the transformative joy of simply READING.<br /><br />We read this at bedtime -- my 12-year-old and I hate-bonded about how bad it was while my 9-year-old was utterly transfixed, so take that as you will. Also, the 12-year-old (and I) figured out really early in the book what the means of escape was going to be so having to WAIT FOR IT was maddening. <br /><br />I don't know how to upload pictures so IMAGINE DONALD SUTHERLAND POINTING AND DOING THAT GRRAAAAAAA THING AT YOU. Oh, hey, I can <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=GEStsLJZhzo" rel="nofollow noopener">LINK!</a><br /><br />ADDENDUM, THREE YEARS LATER: I regret being so bitchy about this book. I loathed it, true, but lemme repeat the part about "my nine-year-old was utterly transfixed," which, jeez, should have been my takeaway. IT IS NOT ALL ABOUT ME; GROW UP, ME. Maxie went on to give this book to her friends for their birthdays, and ALL OF THEM loved it. So, uh, give it to your 9-year-old independent reader and DON'T READ IT ALOUD AT BEDTIME, problem solved. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3868832025720749327" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1981603491" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1981603491" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1981603491?book_show_action=true">Apr 24, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=competition">competition</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1981603491" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10105994403135359262">If you like your reads to be partially interactive, this one’s for you. The interaction is done on the reader’s part, so you can decide not to take part of the game and still enjoy the book, but by playing along with the characters, you become even more invested. <br/><br/>I honestly did not care to play the game along with the characters, because it slowed the pace at which I was reading, but in hindsight, I think I should have, because the rebus is an important element of the story.<br/><br/>Still, I found this t</span>
  <span id="freeText10105994403135359262" style="display:none">If you like your reads to be partially interactive, this one’s for you. The interaction is done on the reader’s part, so you can decide not to take part of the game and still enjoy the book, but by playing along with the characters, you become even more invested. <br /><br />I honestly did not care to play the game along with the characters, because it slowed the pace at which I was reading, but in hindsight, I think I should have, because the rebus is an important element of the story.<br /><br />Still, I found this to be highly addictive and simply a breath of fresh air. There’s always something going on in the story, and there’s a clear progression in regards to both the storyline and game. I enjoyed seeing the later divide people, only to bring them back together later in the game.<br /><br />The characters aren’t complex, but I wouldn’t accuse them of being one-dimensional. It’s true that we lack background on them—except for a few exceptions—but their personalities are distinct.<br /><br />This book could have been about Mr. Lemoncello alone and I still would have read it. He’s that great. His personality is unique and he’s just so much fun. I often wanted to know what was inside his head. He was surprising and a delightful man to be around. <br /><br />What a treasurable book that promotes board games. I’ll be sure to read it again in a few years and this time around invest myself much more in the game. <br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="10105994403135359262" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <a title="Brina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2933855-brina"><img alt="Brina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601675085p2/2933855.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1536148430?book_show_action=true">Feb 03, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brina" href="/user/show/2933855-brina">Brina</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2933855-brina?shelf=ohio">ohio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2933855-brina?shelf=kids">kids</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1536148430" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6688954067873943101">Lately I have been on an easy reading kick. I think I get this way every late winter. That being said, my kids had this book from the library for a reread and told me it is a great book and I should read it. I give this 4.5 stars because it is a great kids book, but to paraphrase my daughter, nothing is as good as Harry Potter. <br/>Escape from Mr. Lemoncello's Library is a fun book for middle grade kids. The town of Alexandriaville, Ohio has not had a public library in 12 years, and millionaire toy </span>
  <span id="freeText6688954067873943101" style="display:none">Lately I have been on an easy reading kick. I think I get this way every late winter. That being said, my kids had this book from the library for a reread and told me it is a great book and I should read it. I give this 4.5 stars because it is a great kids book, but to paraphrase my daughter, nothing is as good as Harry Potter. <br />Escape from Mr. Lemoncello's Library is a fun book for middle grade kids. The town of Alexandriaville, Ohio has not had a public library in 12 years, and millionaire toy maker Luigi Lemoncello has sponsored a new, state of the art library. For a grand opening he has invited 12 twelve year olds to spend the night and then take part in a survivor type game to escape from the library. The winner will get to star in his tv commercials. <br />Our protagonist is Kyle Keeley the younger brother to overachieving Curtis and sports star Mike. Lost in their limelight, Kyle finally has his turn to shine as he takes part in the library escape. As he forms an alliance with his friends, Kyle works to solve Lemoncello's clues in order to win the game. <br />I admit I was not a Willy Wonka fan as a kid so I can't compare the two books. Being the book worm that I am, I enjoyed the state of the art library, the references to classic and contemporary kids books, and the Dewey decimal system. I also thought it was refreshing to see kids working together positively. <br />I would recommend this book to older elementary aged kids, even those who don't read much. It is a fun read and will hopefully encourage kids to read more than they had been before reading this book.</span>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer820534671" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1035009804440928320">This is a messy, loud book crammed full of one-note characters, dizzying book references, and an illogical plot. There is no nuance, no suspense, and no character growth. This is the story of a puzzle, not the story of the people solving it - much to the book's detriment. <i>The Westing Game</i> would be a better choice; in fact, it's entirely possible that book was name-dropped in this one. There were so many awkward book references shoehorned into the story that I honestly couldn't keep track.<br/><br/>And I'm</span>
  <span id="freeText1035009804440928320" style="display:none">This is a messy, loud book crammed full of one-note characters, dizzying book references, and an illogical plot. There is no nuance, no suspense, and no character growth. This is the story of a puzzle, not the story of the people solving it - much to the book's detriment. <i>The Westing Game</i> would be a better choice; in fact, it's entirely possible that book was name-dropped in this one. There were so many awkward book references shoehorned into the story that I honestly couldn't keep track.<br /><br />And I'm confused as to why a library would need a director of holographic imagery. Just buy more books. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12905126907554858939">I cannot understand all the 4 star reviews and the NY Times best seller status of this book. Then again, most of what I find on the children's best seller list lately is mediocre junk!<br/><br/>This is yet another rip-off of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4273.Roald_Dahl' title='Roald Dahl' rel='nofollow noopener'>Roald Dahl</a>'s immortal <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6310.Charlie_and_the_Chocolate_Factory__Charlie_Bucket___1_' title='Charlie and the Chocolate Factory (Charlie Bucket, #1) by Roald Dahl' rel='nofollow noopener'>Charlie and the Chocolate Factory</a>, complete with an eccentric inventor and a contest, only this time with a superduper library instead of a factory.<br/><br/>Here there is one "bad" kid, plus a few others who have their faults, and while they don't meet heinous fates, they</span>
  <span id="freeText12905126907554858939" style="display:none">I cannot understand all the 4 star reviews and the NY Times best seller status of this book. Then again, most of what I find on the children's best seller list lately is mediocre junk!<br /><br />This is yet another rip-off of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4273.Roald_Dahl" title="Roald Dahl" rel="nofollow noopener">Roald Dahl</a>'s immortal <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6310.Charlie_and_the_Chocolate_Factory__Charlie_Bucket___1_" title="Charlie and the Chocolate Factory (Charlie Bucket, #1) by Roald Dahl" rel="nofollow noopener">Charlie and the Chocolate Factory</a>, complete with an eccentric inventor and a contest, only this time with a superduper library instead of a factory.<br /><br />Here there is one "bad" kid, plus a few others who have their faults, and while they don't meet heinous fates, they all lose. The winners, of course, are the "good" kids, plus one who could go either way, but proves to be a "good" kid in the end. Luigi Lemoncello is no match for Willy Wonka, and the endless, ENDLESS insertion of book titles or references is as irritating as product placement in a movie.<br /><br />And yes, there is a "Wonka" reference, but to add insult to injury it's to the movie--and probably to the crappy remake with Johnny Depp!<br /><br />Utterly, utterly, predictable. Is it the libary/reading theme that is making all the librarians and educators kvell?<br /><br />P.S. The technological references will help this book go stale in no time flat.<br /><br />P.P.S. Want a great book that does have a Wonka vibe in that it is about kids and a candy factory contest, and isn't as funny as a Dahl book, but is a lot deeper? <div id="review_699576473" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/699576473" />
    <a title="Kate" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12293609-kate"><img alt="Kate" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1399171915p2/12293609.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/699576473?book_show_action=true">Aug 20, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kate" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kate" href="/user/show/12293609-kate">Kate</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12293609-kate?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12293609-kate?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12293609-kate?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer699576473" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12228549049734124719">You know, I think Grabenstein missed an opportunity to have a great book instead of just a good one. The puzzles and mysteries were fantastically well-placed and a lot of fun to try to solve alongside Kyle and his friends, and I liked the positive teamwork message the book had to send. As a librarian, I absolutely adored the positive library portrayal, the fact that it was a place that was fun and exciting and the clever way the Dewey Decimal system was used in the book. <br/><br/>But to an extent, it see</span>
  <span id="freeText12228549049734124719" style="display:none">You know, I think Grabenstein missed an opportunity to have a great book instead of just a good one. The puzzles and mysteries were fantastically well-placed and a lot of fun to try to solve alongside Kyle and his friends, and I liked the positive teamwork message the book had to send. As a librarian, I absolutely adored the positive library portrayal, the fact that it was a place that was fun and exciting and the clever way the Dewey Decimal system was used in the book. <br /><br />But to an extent, it seemed like that was where Grabenstein stopped trying - with creating the puzzles and mysteries the children had to solve and with incorporating the library aspects. He stopped short of fleshing out the characters much, or giving them any time to do anything other than solve the puzzles or (in the adults' case) hand out clues. This was enjoyable, but I found myself disappointed and wishing that Kyle and his friends had been given the careful treatment that the excellent plot indicated that they deserved.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12228549049734124719" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_671032019" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/671032019" />
    <a title="Kristine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4731250-kristine"><img alt="Kristine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1446697306p2/4731250.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/671032019?book_show_action=true">Jul 18, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristine" href="/user/show/4731250-kristine">Kristine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4731250-kristine?shelf=novel">novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4731250-kristine?shelf=ages-9-to-12">ages-9-to-12</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4731250-kristine?shelf=good-for-boys">good-for-boys</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4731250-kristine?shelf=read-for-my-job">read-for-my-job</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer671032019" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17857726466278298148">Whenever I see a book about a library, I tend to order it for the collection at my library. This was one of the best things to come from this whim! Perfect for both the reluctant reader and avid bibliophile, <i>Escape From Mr. Lemoncello's Library</i> had me hooked even as an adult.<br/><br/>Twelve 12-year-olds are selected for an overnight experience at their new public library. Little do they know, this is actually a set-up for the time of their lives. When the overnight is over, they find themselves locked-in</span>
  <span id="freeText17857726466278298148" style="display:none">Whenever I see a book about a library, I tend to order it for the collection at my library. This was one of the best things to come from this whim! Perfect for both the reluctant reader and avid bibliophile, <i>Escape From Mr. Lemoncello's Library</i> had me hooked even as an adult.<br /><br />Twelve 12-year-olds are selected for an overnight experience at their new public library. Little do they know, this is actually a set-up for the time of their lives. When the overnight is over, they find themselves locked-in. Their only hope is to figure out the clues and piece together the puzzles in order to win the ultimate prize.<br /><br />Kyle was a great character. Realistically flawed yet a good role model for readers. The peripheral characters were also charmingly well-developed and really added to the story. Plus, where to even start on the setting? It was spectacularly fantastical, mixing just enough eccentricity in with reality to make it extraordinarily possible. I only hope kids aren't disappointed when their own libraries aren't quite as amazing (which is a mostly sarcastic observation).<br /><br />I loved the seamless way learning was woven into the story. There is so much to discover about Dewey classification, the help librarians offer, and the fun that reading can be. Grabenstein's description of the kids getting caught up reading about Sherlock was almost tangible. This is children's literature, but it's not lazy in the least. Yet it's also completely accessible. It was fast-paced and had a good flow to it.<br /><br />As others have mentioned, it reminded me of a cross between <i>The Westing Game</i> and <i>Charlie and the Chocolate Factory</i>. However, I think I enjoyed this one more as it didn't have the pretentious, dark edge those two presented (more so the latter). This was just a fun jaunt through the library with a good heart, great lessons, and fun for all!</span>
  <a data-text-id="17857726466278298148" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16733095-bennett?shelf=childrens-and-mg">childrens-and-mg</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer690809447" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13823879900221734455"><b>Grade rating: 67% D</b><br/><br/>A super huge library is any book lover's dream! But this or comes with a catch...<br/><br/>I didn't really like this one.<br/><br/>The author was annoying, first of all. He was trying to make his characters seem like the kids of today. When Charles said "I'll Twitter it", my spine shuddered is disgust. Also, the author kept making references to books. New books, not just the classics. I don't think references to recent literature should <i>never</i> happen, but I feel it's out of place. That got annoyin</span>
  <span id="freeText13823879900221734455" style="display:none"><b>Grade rating: 67% D</b><br /><br />A super huge library is any book lover's dream! But this or comes with a catch...<br /><br />I didn't really like this one.<br /><br />The author was annoying, first of all. He was trying to make his characters seem like the kids of today. When Charles said "I'll Twitter it", my spine shuddered is disgust. Also, the author kept making references to books. New books, not just the classics. I don't think references to recent literature should <i>never</i> happen, but I feel it's out of place. That got annoying real quick.<br /><br />Second, it was so predictable. Kyle's team won, blah blah blah. The book needed more twists. Wouldn't it be better if Haley revealed at the end that she joined Kyle's team just to get the answers and win, because her want of being a commercial star consumed her? That would have been amazing. Also, the narrator should have focused on each character equally, and there shouldn't have been teams, so you didn't know who would win.<br /><br />At the beginning, Sierra was my kind of character. Shy, bookish, and quiet. Then she joined a team and that all went away. She became someone she wasn't. No. That's not right. I was positive she would win because she was the underdog. Also, Charles's elimination was meaningless. If he broke a rule a long time ago in the game, why did they take him out of the game just then? Unbelievable. He should have been there until the end, then Kyle's team would pull ahead and Charles would lose.<br /><br />In the end, an odd little story with annoyances everywhere and un-needed references. There were plenty of other book I would have rather been reading.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13823879900221734455" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38617426-juli?shelf=read-audiobooks-2019">read-audiobooks-2019</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2075625538" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11469163396299087915">What a wonderful, imaginative, and creative story! This book totally reminded me why I still love to read children's books! <br/><br/>After several years without a city library, a new wonderous library has been built by an ecentric, quirky billionaire...Mr. Lemoncello. Kyle and his school friends are familiar with Mr. Lemoncello as his company has made many of their favorite boardgames, including Mr. Lemoncello's Indoor Outdoor Scavenger Hunt. At school, they write essays for a contest -- the winners get </span>
  <span id="freeText11469163396299087915" style="display:none">What a wonderful, imaginative, and creative story! This book totally reminded me why I still love to read children's books! <br /><br />After several years without a city library, a new wonderous library has been built by an ecentric, quirky billionaire...Mr. Lemoncello. Kyle and his school friends are familiar with Mr. Lemoncello as his company has made many of their favorite boardgames, including Mr. Lemoncello's Indoor Outdoor Scavenger Hunt. At school, they write essays for a contest -- the winners get to see the new library before anybody else. It's the adventure of a lifetime! <br /><br />For me, this story was reminiscent of Willy Wonka and the Chocolate Factory with a library theme instead of a candy factory. The characters are fun and quirky....and there's lots of book references and library goodness. Fun story! <br /><br />I was delighted to find out that there is a television movie version, streamable on Hulu. I'm going to watch it as soon as I post this review. :) Following my rule: Always read the book first! I'm not quite sure how they are going to capture the magic of this story in only 69 minutes though.....the movie must cut out a lot. I hope I'm not disappointed. <br /><br />I listened to the audio book version of this story. The audio is almost 6.5 hours long and narrated by Jesse Bernstein. Bernstein reads at a nice pace and does a great job bringing the characters to life. Excellent performance! <br /><br />There are 3 other books in the Lemoncello series so far. Chris Grabenstein has written several books for middle grade kids. I'm definitely going to be reading more! Loved this story!</span>

<div id="review_2460525335" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2460525335" />
    <a title="Sandy *The world could end while I was reading and I would never notice*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30817744-sandy-the-world-could-end-while-i-was-reading-and-i-would-never-notice"><img alt="Sandy *The world could end while I was reading and I would never notice*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1509647506p2/30817744.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sandy *The world could end while I was reading and I would never notice*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sandy *The world could end while I was reading and I would never notice*" href="/user/show/30817744-sandy-the-world-could-end-while-i-was-reading-and-i-would-never-notice">Sandy *The world could end while I was reading and I would never notice*</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30817744-sandy-the-world-could-end-while-i-was-reading-and-i-would-never-notice?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30817744-sandy-the-world-could-end-while-i-was-reading-and-i-would-never-notice?shelf=4-star">4-star</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2460525335" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5825835001551724954">EXCERPT: So Kyle had gone down to the basement and dug up one of his all-time favorites: Mr Lemoncello's Indoor Outdoor Scavenger Hunt. It had been a huge hit for Mr Lemoncello, the master game maker. Kyle and his brothers had played it so much when they were younger, Mrs Keeley wrote to Mr Lemoncello's company for a refresher pack of clue cards. The new cards listed all kinds of different bizarre stuff you needed to find, like 'an adults droopy underpants', 'one dirty dish' and 'a rotten banana</span>
  <span id="freeText5825835001551724954" style="display:none">EXCERPT: So Kyle had gone down to the basement and dug up one of his all-time favorites: Mr Lemoncello's Indoor Outdoor Scavenger Hunt. It had been a huge hit for Mr Lemoncello, the master game maker. Kyle and his brothers had played it so much when they were younger, Mrs Keeley wrote to Mr Lemoncello's company for a refresher pack of clue cards. The new cards listed all kinds of different bizarre stuff you needed to find, like 'an adults droopy underpants', 'one dirty dish' and 'a rotten banana peel'.<br /><br />(At the end of the game, the losers have to put everything back exactly where the items had been found. It was an official rule, printed inside the top of the box, and made winning the game that much more important!)<br /><br />ABOUT THIS BOOK: Kyle Keeley is the class clown, popular with most kids, (if not the teachers), and an ardent fan of all games: board games, word games, and particularly video games. His hero, Luigi Lemoncello, the most notorious and creative gamemaker in the world, just so happens to be the genius behind the building of the new town library.<br /><br />Lucky Kyle wins a coveted spot to be one of the first 12 kids in the library for an overnight of fun, food, and lots and lots of games. But when morning comes, the doors remain locked. Kyle and the other winners must solve every clue and every secret puzzle to find the hidden escape route. And the stakes are very high.<br /><br />MY THOUGHTS: School holiday time here in New Zealand, and traditionally the time for my grandson and I to do our buddy read. You may remember that last year we read our way through the Harry Potter series. Our time was curtailed somewhat these holidays as he spent the first week in the South Island skiing. But last week we read two books together, and this was the first of them, and his pick. <br /><br />This was a fun read which teaches lessons about the perils of cheating, the advantages of learning to work as part of a team, and how to think outside the box (or the most obvious answer is not always the correct one).<br /><br />Honestly, neither of us could see what was wrong with being locked in a library, particularly since this library has a café, and we would have been quite happy to have stayed there. But this book was not about us. <br /><br />We did enjoy trying to solve the puzzles, though we (or more specifically I) weren't all that successful. <br /><br />My grandson thought that this ultra modern library would be wonderful. Me? I have fond memories of the library of my childhood (now sadly demolished), a grand old wooden building with coke fuelled fires that I would curl up in front of and read for hours. And wonderful librarians, one of whom is still alive and whom I visit whenever I can. <br /><br />Escape from Mr Lemoncello's Library fuelled a lot of discussion between us. My grandson now knows a lot more about my life as a child, and the books I read. He has some new titles to read, as do I. And while he has already read the other books in this series, I haven't, but am keen to do so. <br /><br />😍😍😍😍<br /><br />THE AUTHOR: CHRIS GRABENSTEIN is a #1 New York Times bestselling. His books include the LEMONCELLO LIBRARY series, the WONDERLAND series, and many fun and funny page-turners co-authored with James Patterson. You can visit Chris at ChrisGrabenstein.com.<br /><br />DISCLOSURE: I listened to Escape from Mr Lemoncello's Library by Chris Grabenstein, narrated by Jesse Bernstein and published by Listening Library via OverDrive. All opinions expressed in this review are entirely my own personal opinions. <br /><br />Please refer to my Goodreads.com profile page or the 'about' page on sandysbookaday.wordpress.com for an explanation of my rating system. <br /><br />This review and others are also published on my blog sandysbookaday.wordpress.com <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://sandysbookaday.wordpress.com/2018/07/24/escape-from-mr-lemoncellos-library-by-chris-grabenstein/">https://sandysbookaday.wordpress.com/...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="5825835001551724954" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_636860630" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/636860630" />
    <a title="Callie *Fights Censorship*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2693106-callie-fights-censorship"><img alt="Callie *Fights Censorship*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577987678p2/2693106.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/636860630?book_show_action=true">Jun 09, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Callie *Fights Censorship*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Callie *Fights Censorship*" href="/user/show/2693106-callie-fights-censorship">Callie *Fights Censorship*</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9780804168083" href="/book/show/18119450-escape-from-mr-lemoncello-s-library">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2693106-callie-fights-censorship?shelf=worst-book-ever">worst-book-ever</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2693106-callie-fights-censorship?shelf=terrible-writing">terrible-writing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2693106-callie-fights-censorship?shelf=audio-book">audio-book</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer636860630" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2311678281173507193">First off are <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/46474.Patrick_Carman' title='Patrick Carman' rel='nofollow noopener'>Patrick Carman</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/95190.Chris_Grabenstein' title='Chris Grabenstein' rel='nofollow noopener'>Chris Grabenstein</a> secretly the same person? <br/><br/>Are they twins?<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1396818101ra/9190746.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Their books felt so similar and not just because they were very poorly done Willy Wonka knockoffs. Both <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10284337.Floors' title='Floors by Patrick Carman' rel='nofollow noopener'>Floors</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16054808.Escape_from_Mr__Lemoncello_s_Library__Mr__Lemoncello_s_Library__1_' title='Escape from Mr. Lemoncello's Library (Mr. Lemoncello's Library #1) by Chris Grabenstein' rel='nofollow noopener'>Escape from Mr. Lemoncello's Library</a> have shallow cardboard characters that spout out terribly unrealistic dialogue. Their plots are boring and consist of very little story beyond having a setting filled with over the top technology. They both strive to be witty and whimsical, and both fail, </span>
  <span id="freeText2311678281173507193" style="display:none">First off are <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/46474.Patrick_Carman" title="Patrick Carman" rel="nofollow noopener">Patrick Carman</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/95190.Chris_Grabenstein" title="Chris Grabenstein" rel="nofollow noopener">Chris Grabenstein</a> secretly the same person? <br><br>Are they twins?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1396818101ra/9190746.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Their books felt so similar and not just because they were very poorly done Willy Wonka knockoffs. Both <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10284337.Floors" title="Floors by Patrick Carman" rel="nofollow noopener">Floors</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16054808.Escape_from_Mr__Lemoncello_s_Library__Mr__Lemoncello_s_Library__1_" title="Escape from Mr. Lemoncello's Library (Mr. Lemoncello's Library #1) by Chris Grabenstein" rel="nofollow noopener">Escape from Mr. Lemoncello's Library</a> have shallow cardboard characters that spout out terribly unrealistic dialogue. Their plots are boring and consist of very little story beyond having a setting filled with over the top technology. They both strive to be witty and whimsical, and both fail, miserably.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1394501242ra/8861809.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <br><br>This book is an abomination, I am having a hard time accepting the average rating on this book, I am in disbelief as I look at all the 5 star ratings!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1399661798ra/9579841.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The plot of this book is so stupid. A bunch of kids get to spend the night in a crazy library and are then abandoned by all the adults, locked in for the entire weekend, and watched from security cameras. But guess what! If they can escape from the library they will be in a bunch of commercials, um okay? There is absolutely no risk and not much of a reward. Plus the game seems completely rigged, the team of 'bad kids' seem unfairly punished and the 'good kids' get bonus clues for absolutely no reason. Gee I wonder what the outcome of this extremely uninteresting scenario with be....? <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1396821323ra/9191087.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>What really makes this book awful is the LARGE cast of nothing characters.<br><br><b>Lemoncello</b> Ugh! This guy is the worst, so incredibly annoying. Here we have an eccentric bazillionaire who decides to spend 500 million on a library for his hometown. He is so wacky, he wears rubber chicken shoes that squeak out POP GOES THE WEASLEY, wow what a wild and crazy guy. He uses tons of out of place literary references and sounds like an after school special most of the time. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1396819220ra/9190846.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Kyle</b> He's our main character and the person we should be rooting for, except I'm not sure why? He has two younger brothers and enjoys playing board games and watching re-runs of Miami Vice, why? Because it is convenient for the plot, duh! Oh and even though this is a library competition, Kyle never reads, that's why he aligns himself with Sierra.<br><br><b>Sierra</b> She likes to read. Apparently she knows everything, literally. Our characters never even have to GOOGLE, they have this convenient plot device who can speed up the process. Never mind that she is 12 years old. For example, one character wonders what event happened on Feb. 20, 1915 and Sierra literally responds immediately <i>oh that was was the day the The Panama–Pacific International Exposition opened in San Francisco, California. Sorry I'm a big fan of World Fairs</i> I actually had to laugh out loud it is so ridiculous. Even Hermione had to look stuff up in the library!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1396994697ra/9215888.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><b>Charles</b> He's the bad kid. He's bad because he's rich and wants to win the game. Wow what a jerk!<br><br><b>Haley</b> She is the one character that I actually thought deserved to win, but the reader is apparently supposed to hate her, at least at the start. I guess we are supposed to see her as a spoiled brat, even though she isn't. In fact she is actually going through a pretty hard time since her dad lost his job and her mother has been reduced to stealing food, she could have been the most interesting character but she is a girl who just wants attention, ugh! Girls are the worst when they try to be pretty and stuff.<br><br>Then there are a whole bunch of other characters that are just as forgettable and stale.<br><br>If you are going to market your book as a <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6310.Charlie_and_the_Chocolate_Factory__Charlie_Bucket___1_" title="Charlie and the Chocolate Factory (Charlie Bucket, #1) by Roald Dahl" rel="nofollow noopener">Charlie and the Chocolate Factory</a> read-a-like and even reference the original in your story you are setting yourself up for comparison. Unfortunately, there is no comparison, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4273.Roald_Dahl" title="Roald Dahl" rel="nofollow noopener">Roald Dahl</a> was a genius. he understood how to write for children. He understood that children like to be scared but they don't like to be talked down to. <br><br>Being inspired is one thing but you have to take the concept and make it your own, make it fresh, at the very least you have to make it interesting. This book was devoid of danger. There was no suspense, nothing was at risk. With Wonka you are wondering is this guy insane? Is this factory dangerous? What is happening to these children that are disappearing? With this knock off every problem is solved immediately. There is no moral to the story and the child reading at home has learned nothing substantial except for the occasional bit of trivia.<br><br>And the ending....<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The whole everyone's a winner thing is garbage! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Thanks for wasting my time!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1396994697ra/9215889.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="2311678281173507193" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_757663169" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/757663169" />
    <a title="Chelsea" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1599836-chelsea"><img alt="Chelsea" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1382730044p2/1599836.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/757663169?book_show_action=true">Nov 05, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea" href="/user/show/1599836-chelsea">Chelsea</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer757663169" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12216649357184146501">A fun, entertaining read. Unfortunately, some people might decide not to bother with reading this book since it seems too reminiscent of "Charlie and the Chocolate Factory." But before you make any hasty decisions, I'm glad to inform you Chris Grabenstein readily addresses the similarities and in quite an amusing manner. There were multiple references to books scattered throughout, which I found quite delightful. How could you not enjoy a book that's meant to teach children the wonderful joys an</span>
  <span id="freeText12216649357184146501" style="display:none">A fun, entertaining read. Unfortunately, some people might decide not to bother with reading this book since it seems too reminiscent of "Charlie and the Chocolate Factory." But before you make any hasty decisions, I'm glad to inform you Chris Grabenstein readily addresses the similarities and in quite an amusing manner. There were multiple references to books scattered throughout, which I found quite delightful. How could you not enjoy a book that's meant to teach children the wonderful joys and hidden treasures contained within a public library? <br /><br />Technology was woven throughout this book, but it was done in such a manner that showed how it can be used for good and not bad. I guess sometimes technology is considered so much more exciting than books it makes me worry what the future may hold. I wonder if one day kids will forgo books entirely for video games. Luckily, this book gave me the hope to think otherwise. I really enjoyed seeing Kyle's interest in reading flourish. It didn't take him too long to realize books are just as good as "watching a 3-D IMAX movie in his head."<br /><br />I thought some of the trivia and questions might be pretty hard for 12 year olds, especially considering most kids nowadays don't even know the slightest thing about "Hawaii Five-O" or Agatha Christie. Shoot, some of the questions were hard for <i>me</i>! I could be wrong though ;p. <br /><br />There were a lot of good messages scattered throughout this book as well. I won't spoil them for you, but I was glad to see there were repercussions and rewards for the children's behavior. The riddles were truly enjoyable and I found myself scrambling to figure them out as well.<br /><br />If you love books, then "Escape from Mr. Lemoncello's Library" is a definite must read!<br /><br />P.S. - There's even an unsolved mystery mentioned at the end of the book! I'm working on figuring it out, but it's certainly a bit of a challenge. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12216649357184146501" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer756803784" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3757618458361488265">Mr. Lemoncello has the coolest library on the face of the planet! Sigh. Too bad it isn't a real place. Kyle and his friends win a chance to be the first to experience the new library and play some fun games. Mr. Lemoncello is, after all, a game creating genius. But the overnighter takes an unexpected turn when the door won't open in the morning and a new game is introduced. The game requires those who participate to find an alternative exit to the library, but they only have 24 hours to do it. K</span>
  <span id="freeText3757618458361488265" style="display:none">Mr. Lemoncello has the coolest library on the face of the planet! Sigh. Too bad it isn't a real place. Kyle and his friends win a chance to be the first to experience the new library and play some fun games. Mr. Lemoncello is, after all, a game creating genius. But the overnighter takes an unexpected turn when the door won't open in the morning and a new game is introduced. The game requires those who participate to find an alternative exit to the library, but they only have 24 hours to do it. Kyle and his friends must decide how to approach the game using only the resources in the library and each other. But will they work together and share the prize or alone?<br /><br />Strengths: I loved the library in this book, it sounds absolutely awesome, with lots of bells and whistles as well as the books themselves. Kyle is a fun, nice kid who tries to do the right thing even when it is disadvantageous. The puzzles are fabulous and I enjoyed them a great deal. The references to literature are great as well. While a lot of kids might not recognize some of the book references the book is till very enjoyable and they should get at least a few of them. Loved this one!<br /><br />Weaknesses: Didn't see many, except maybe the references to adult literature, but the book can be enjoyed even without knowing all the books that are referred to.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14141912755899128834">Rating: 3.75* of five, rounded up because DAMN!<br/><br/>Want to know something? I read this book *after* its sequel! Want to know something else? I hate reading Young Readers books! And guess what? No, you guess, c'mon! C'mon, please? Oh okay: I did NOT hate reading this book OR its sequel!<br/><br/>I know, right?<br/><br/>Chris Grabenstein writes for middle-graders like a middle-grader would, and I mean that as a compliment. He gets right into the mindset of a young person in a way that I don't see a lot of adult writers d</span>
  <span id="freeText14141912755899128834" style="display:none">Rating: 3.75* of five, rounded up because DAMN!<br /><br />Want to know something? I read this book *after* its sequel! Want to know something else? I hate reading Young Readers books! And guess what? No, you guess, c'mon! C'mon, please? Oh okay: I did NOT hate reading this book OR its sequel!<br /><br />I know, right?<br /><br />Chris Grabenstein writes for middle-graders like a middle-grader would, and I mean that as a compliment. He gets right into the mindset of a young person in a way that I don't see a lot of adult writers doing. He anticipates the questions a younger reader is most likely going to ask and, before they can even be posed consciously, leads the reader to the answer while making it seem they've gotten ahead of the author. That's quality writing for any age, let alone the finicky and detail-oriented 9-to-12 market.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14141912755899128834" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2179505092" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer17824883209610170773">I’m a fan of Willy Wonka. I’m also a fan of The Westing Game, Night in the Museum, National Treasure, and the first Brixton Brothers book. This book had elements of all of these and ended up being pretty fun. :D<br/><br/>Okay, libraries are pretty cool to start with, but I’m not sure any can compare to this one. There’s a hoverboard for checking out books on higher shelves, holographic statues, and huge screens on the ceiling to represent the Dewey decimal system. And much more. At first, especially durin</span>
  <span id="freeText17824883209610170773" style="display:none">I’m a fan of Willy Wonka. I’m also a fan of The Westing Game, Night in the Museum, National Treasure, and the first Brixton Brothers book. This book had elements of all of these and ended up being pretty fun. :D<br /><br />Okay, libraries are pretty cool to start with, but I’m not sure any can compare to this one. There’s a hoverboard for checking out books on higher shelves, holographic statues, and huge screens on the ceiling to represent the Dewey decimal system. And much more. At first, especially during the construction scenes, I had trouble picturing the library since it is pretty bizarre, but after awhile I was able to build a picture in my head. ;) <br /><br />The games were very fun and clever, though not too hard that a middle-grade reader couldn’t enjoy trying to solve them along with the characters. There were a ton of literary references too. :D :D Mr. Lemoncello talks almost entirely in book titles, and reading a couple Sherlock Holmes’ short stories helped the characters figure out a clue. (A+ for that!) Mrs. Tobin is <i>the</i> classic librarian. <br /><br />I really liked the concept of learning to appreciate and use all the tools a library has to offer. (I think we miss what a goldmine they are sometimes.) I feel like I should learn the Dewey decimal system now. XD The characters were pretty cool, and Kyle was a great protagonist. My favorite part though was how compassion, teamwork, and determination were what in the end won the game. (Thanks to some bonus clues. :D) <br /><br />Just a note, there are a few instances of mean children and a couple slang words.<br /><br />Best quote: “Congratulations, Rose!” cried Mr. Lemoncello, who had put on a pointy party hat. “For sticking to your prior commitments, you will receive our special Prior Commitment Sticker prize: a complete set of Lemoncello Sticker Picture Games and a laptop computer to play them on! Enjoy.”<br /><br />Altogether, this book kept me amused and guessing. ;)<br /></span>

<div id="review_641361911" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/641361911" />
    <a title="Heather" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1236786-heather"><img alt="Heather" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1311903137p2/1236786.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/641361911?book_show_action=true">Jun 14, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heather" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heather" href="/user/show/1236786-heather">Heather</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1236786-heather?shelf=kids-books-i-would-recommend">kids-books-i-would-recommend</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1236786-heather?shelf=2013">2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer641361911" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14129031640909282685"><i>Review of an advance copy:</i><br/><br/>I'm breaking a 5-month Goodreads hiatus to post my review of this excellent book. I was fortunate enough to receive an advance copy and the kids at my library will be able to read the final version in only 11 days. I can't wait to hear their reactions! :)<br/><br/>So, for starters, <i>Escape from Mr. Lemoncello's Library</i> is brilliant. It has all the wonder, imagination, and wackiness of Willy Wonka's chocolate factory or Merganzer Whippet's hotel (Patrick Carman's <i>Floors</i>), and yet i</span>
  <span id="freeText14129031640909282685" style="display:none"><i>Review of an advance copy:</i><br /><br />I'm breaking a 5-month Goodreads hiatus to post my review of this excellent book. I was fortunate enough to receive an advance copy and the kids at my library will be able to read the final version in only 11 days. I can't wait to hear their reactions! :)<br /><br />So, for starters, <i>Escape from Mr. Lemoncello's Library</i> is brilliant. It has all the wonder, imagination, and wackiness of Willy Wonka's chocolate factory or Merganzer Whippet's hotel (Patrick Carman's <i>Floors</i>), and yet it takes place in a library. As the 12 competitors try to solve the puzzle, they (and the reader) are confronted with some very clever codes, clues, and rebuses. The hunt takes them all over the library, so they learn about authors, books, and Dewey Decimal Classification. At the same time, though, the information is so well-placed that readers won't even realize they are learning. Like Kyle, though, they may have a list of books they'd like to look at once they finish this one! <br /><br />The book emphasizes teamwork, loyalty, fair play, reading, libraries, puzzles, and problem-solving. It is very fast-paced, as the competition takes place over a 24-hour period, and I can't picture any kid finding it unexciting. It is also quite amusing. I particularly enjoyed the fabulous puns using book titles that our wacky game maker, Mr. Lemoncello, comes up with.<br /><br />I would recommend <i>Escape from Mr. Lemoncello's Library</i> to fans of <i>Charlie and the Chocolate Factory</i>, <i>Floors</i>, <i>The Westing Game</i>, and fans of mystery and adventure in general. Frankly, I would recommend it to any kid. It fits in any public, school, or home library. It would be great fun for family or classroom reading as well as individual reading. It's a perfect book to take to the beach or on a summer road trip, too. <br /><br />Kids who read this book will wish they could visit Alexandriaville's new public library. I sure did! And librarians should be prepared for fans of life-size games (life-size chess, Clue, etc.) to request to play a version of Mr. Lemoncello's game. I'm already trying to figure out how we could make this ultimate scavenger hunt/clue search/adventure work at my library. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14129031640909282685" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_651327217" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/651327217" />
    <a title="Susan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/351657-susan"><img alt="Susan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1586475210p2/351657.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/651327217?book_show_action=true">Jun 25, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Susan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Susan" href="/user/show/351657-susan">Susan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/351657-susan?shelf=juvenile">juvenile</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer651327217" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6181454934000149770">+ 1/2 star just because it's hard to feel too snarky about a book that so unabashedly oozes such love for libraries and games.<br/><br/>I think this is the book that my 8-12 year-old self had always hoped for--if I could have written a book then it would be something like the world in this book. Some of my favorite books back then incorporated quirkiness and puzzles and word play. I loved the <i>Westing Game</i> and <i>The Phantom Tollbooth</i> and I wanted to love this book--because how could you not love the idea of </span>
  <span id="freeText6181454934000149770" style="display:none">+ 1/2 star just because it's hard to feel too snarky about a book that so unabashedly oozes such love for libraries and games.<br /><br />I think this is the book that my 8-12 year-old self had always hoped for--if I could have written a book then it would be something like the world in this book. Some of my favorite books back then incorporated quirkiness and puzzles and word play. I loved the <i>Westing Game</i> and <i>The Phantom Tollbooth</i> and I wanted to love this book--because how could you not love the idea of a group of kids locked in at a library overnight, competing in this epic challenge competition where they get to live out a board game? <br /><br />The thing is though, with Raskin, and Dahl, and Konigsburg is there was always sort of an underlying edge somewhere-some poignancy, or a little darkness, or a wry little twist. Heck, Dahl could be pretty freaking disturbing when he wanted to be. There's a reason Johnny Depp was a little off-putting as Willy Wonka, and also a reason that Gene Wilder immortalized the role. He perfected that weirdly fine line between giddiness and cynicism by balancing his own good natured affability and sweetness with the Willy Wonka bite. In contrast, Mr. Lemoncello (and his book) are basically Gene Wilder sans bite. The game guru is basically just an overgrown kid in a candy store-or in this case--a library. Grabenstein was clearly inspired by these other books and authors and references abound, but without the nuance of the shading, all the enthusiasm and giddiness starts to feel a little contrived after awhile. Rather than have the book work so hard to sell the fact that reading is fun and libraries are wondrous places, I think it would make it even better if the game and personalities of the characters could be given a little more detail and distinction.<br /><br />Fans of the Candy Shop Wars could give this a try.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6181454934000149770" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_719549023" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/719549023" />
    <a title="Lauren" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/876373-lauren"><img alt="Lauren" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1358742153p2/876373.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/719549023?book_show_action=true">Sep 14, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lauren" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lauren" href="/user/show/876373-lauren">Lauren</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/876373-lauren?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer719549023" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8943645017369773421">I loved this book! To me, it was a love letter to libraries and books in general. As a librarian, I loved how Grabenstein showed how much fun finding information can be. I also appreciated that our protagonist Kyle was presented as a non-reader in the beginning, but evolved into a reader by the end after both talking to kids who liked to read and also picking up a book himself. Grabenstein also very cleverly and very subtly inserted a reading list for people who read this book. Several titles ar</span>
  <span id="freeText8943645017369773421" style="display:none">I loved this book! To me, it was a love letter to libraries and books in general. As a librarian, I loved how Grabenstein showed how much fun finding information can be. I also appreciated that our protagonist Kyle was presented as a non-reader in the beginning, but evolved into a reader by the end after both talking to kids who liked to read and also picking up a book himself. Grabenstein also very cleverly and very subtly inserted a reading list for people who read this book. Several titles are mentioned along with short descriptions that would get people interested in them. I made sure to talk to the 5th and 6th graders in my community about this book and I was thrilled at how excited the kids were to check the book out. <br /><br />Taking my librarian hat off, I still enjoyed the book. It had a nice mystery/puzzle for the kids to solve and the characters themselves were pretty interesting as well. There were no "completely good" kids. They all had flaws and I appreciated that not every kid wanted to participate in the escape contest. Some just didn't want to while others had previous commitments. This made the characters seem much more realistic. <br /><br />I would have given this book 5 stars except for two things. One, the villain was a bit over-the-top to the point of being tiresome. Two, there was a portion towards the end that felt a tiny bit like a deus ex machina. On the one hand, it is believable, but on the other hand, it's a tad too convenient. Regardless, it's a fantastic read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8943645017369773421" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mari Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mari Anne" href="/user/show/1663741-mari-anne">Mari Anne</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>
